< review>
Everything about this place was more than expected! Went out to the track for the weekend with the family and noticeably from the entrance this place was cleaner than anyone could expect. Just as some are probably worried about staying in a nasty hotel, this was completely opposite. The kitchen was clean, the bathrooms not a spec, floors were clean, rooms and bed were emaculate. The bed was the most comfortable bed ive ever slept in. The rules while on the property are posted and very clear!  Nice deck you can sit outside and unwind, watch the sun rise or set. I didnt see a place you could BBQ however, I saw other people bring their own BBQ grill and there is a fully equipped kitchen for all your cooking needs. Loved and enjoyed our stay here.
Would definitely recommend this place üèÜ‚ù§

FYI * the office sells approx 20lb bags of ice for 7.00!< /review>

<Rating>5</Rating>< text>
Have been to Chuckwalla Valley Raceway several times with NASA AZ for racing. The Owner and staff are very friendly and helpful. Track is wide, good pavement, plenty of run off for racing and beginner HPDE drivers. Restrooms and showers in paddock area and plenty of space for race trailers, RV's, etc. Bring all your supplies with you, food, water, fuel, etc for the weekend. The nearest gas station is 25 miles and grocery store in 51 miles. Its a long drive from Texas, but planning to go back.<//text>

<rate>5<//rate><text>While I never drove a single mile here, I must say the people of this track are truly wonderful, kind people who helped us when we were completely stranded! We had run out of gas on I-10, and though we'd brought bikes, the closest gas station was 20 miles away. After a few quick calls, we biked down to the track where Warren loaded us into his truck, loaned us a gas can, and sold us the few gallons we were short. Not to leave a job half done, he drove us (and our bikes) back to our Jeep, saving us the return bike ride.

The office lady was also very helpful and the grounds, beautifully maintained. There were several cabins in the front that you could rent, a fenced in dog area, tent camping, and a new motocross track! I'm not a racer, but this place is a little oasis in the Desert Center.</text>< pictures>

<user>116287407152488760730<//user>< Name>
Julia Nai< /Name>
< date>
1625817292886</date>
< Rating>
5< /Rating>
<Text>I really really like this building. If you are thinking of moving in here, I have some points that might be useful as me and my boyfriend were looking through 30+ high rises when we tried to move.
The points in order are gym, spa, roof, service, room amenities,  deliveries, location, things this apartment doesn't have/cons.

- The gym is great. There are a good selection of weight machines and cardio machines as well as ropes and a heavy bag outdoors. There is also a small artificial turf area to pull/push sleds. There isn't a free Olympic weight bar set, but there is a Smith machine with two degrees of freedom rather than the typical one. The gym is open 24/7.
- The spa area is extremely pleasent. There is a steam room and a sauna and a Jacuzzi which are usually not too packed. It closes at 10:00pm right now, but I'm not sure if that is a COVID thing.
- The views are spectacular both from the rooms and from the roof. Speaking of the roof, there is a pool table, shuffle board table, and bocce ball court all overlooking the salesforce tower/park. The views from the roof (35th floor) are absolutely gorgeous and you can sit and study/do work with the wifi up there and look out at any direction around the building.
- The rooms are really nice and the amenities are super modern. There is a gas stove, and in the two br, there is one bath/shower and one huge walk in shower. There is also AC and heating which is suprisingly nice. The balcony is large enough to fit a small table and some chairs (though I must say the height still makes me a little scared). Everything has a really clean modern look, and there is a good amount of space bar the pillar in the middle of the living room that can be a little annoying to plan around (this is for the D apartments).
- The service people are super prompt and friendly. I was surprised when someone showed up at my door to replace a key because I had only submitted the ticket 10 or so minutes prior. The front desk people are also SUPER friendly and very helpful with anything that goes wrong. They were especially nice considering the COVID precautions regarding getting packages.
- Speaking of packages, there is an amazon locker on the first floor that you have to get your packages from and a mail room next to that. But deliveries such as DoorDash, UberEats, or Amazon Prime Now are delivered to your door which is really convenient.
- The location is really quite. We live above a freeway yet cannot hear anything other than the occasional police siren. There are some really great restaurants one or so blocks away, and salesforce park is a great place to walk through on a nice day. And I hope you like walking because parking is $500 a month, but the valet is really nice. And you can rent teslas for $28ish an hour.
- There are some things this apartment doesn't have. There is no pool. There aren't free Olympic bar weight sets. Packages aren't brought to your door. If you have friends visit, there is parking down the street for $20 a day or you can park in valet in the building for $40 a day. You can, if you are very lucky, park on the street, but there is street sweeping Mon, Wed, and Fri and the tickets are painful. There's no Foosball table. The fridge door doesn't have a magnet or any way to close so sometimes it stays slightly open and then beeps forever (this is the ultimate first world problem, I know). Trash gets picked up form your door everyday and you have no option to throw things away yourself down the shoot (whether this is a pro/con is up to you). If it is a busy time of day (Friday nights etc.), or someone is moving, or the it's trash pickup time, the elevators can take quite a bit, but it's (almost) never egregious. There is also little counter space.

Conclusion, I really like this place for all the reasons listed above. We pro/con-ed every high rise within our price range (with our personal criteria), and this came out clearly on top. Granted we got it at a COVID discount, but at the end of our lease, if we decide to stay in San Francisco, we would definitely like to stay here.<//Text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNUABL4L2fePzOpzLV3JKmu-KG6XQmrT--WvRaP=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMS7yKLPMYb_TM-5rg_M7UQBqskYQ99oFD4abVs=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics>< response>

Disclaimer: I never lived in 33 Tehama; this review is purely based on my experiences with the leasing office.

I spent about a month looking for a new place to stay. I didn't end up going with 33 Tehama, mainly because the units were a bit too small for my liking, but everyone in the leasing office was so nice to me that I felt compelled to leave a good review.

<date>1592586021217<//date><rate>3</rate><review>I've been living here for about 10 months now and I think I got a differentiated view on the living experience. So let me first start with the upsides:
+ The apartments are generally pretty and have gorgeous views especially on the higher floors
+ Washer / dryer in unit, large bathrooms and built-in storage cabinets are great
+ The gym equipment and the jacuzzi are great

But unfortunately there are a lot of things here that keep putting a negative touch on the experience:
- Management is highly intransparent and unresponsive once you move in. A few explanations on why I say that. Since COVID-19, all amenities have been closed until further notice. Any questions regarding the timing of reopening are ignored. I tried to post about this on the (management reviewed / censored) community board two or three times and the post never even was put up. Requests to fix small things in the apartment take days. A day after I moved in I realized the closets wouldn't close properly but my ask to have this reflected on my inspection form was ignored and never answered.
- The place is generally overpriced, especially now with COVID. You pay a significant premium for the rooftop, the gym, the spa, valet etc. But while all those services have been cut, the rent has not been adjusted for it, so margin improvements from reduced utility overhead, reduce cleaning and maintenance etc. flow into Greystar's P&L and not back to the customers (questions regarding this have also been blocked from the community portal)
- Many of the staff here are very kind and open, but the leasing staff is grim and don't care about the residents once they move in (a nice smile in the hallway and a hello is not that difficult and should be standard etiquette in a luxury building)

So overall it's a nice building and as an international it's a great opportunity to find a place quickly if you haven't built up your credit score yet. But definitely not a place to stay for long.<//review>< pics>

<text>I have lived in 33 Tehama for 1.5 years when I first moved to SF. I enjoyed my experience here overall. I am moving out soon to a similar building (399 Fremont), but I wanted to offer a hopefully objective review.

Pros
- The rooms are modern and has good amenities (washer&dryer, dish washer, microwave, AC, even cutting boards)
- The room layouts are quite good.
- Maintenance team is awesome! I had issues with my dishwasher (it just fell out one day), toilet clogging and door lock (ran out of battery). I filed a maintenance ticket and the issues were usually resolved within hours.
- The rooftop has great views and I love working from there one day a week (I ended up meeting one of my best friends here), Sauna, hot tub, gym are quite nice.
- The cleaning staff are extremely friendly and hard working.
- Cute dogs live in this building.
- Hello Alfred service is pretty nice. We like asking them to do our groceries. They also do a quick tidy-up which often brightens my day.

Things I didn't quite like:

- Noise. I get woken up at 4am on most nights. My room faces Tehama St, and the H rooms are right above the loading dock. Almost every day, an extremely loud truck comes by at 11pm and 4-5am to collect trash and load construction materials. This wakes me up on most nights, even when we shut all our windows and doors. My husband is a quite heavy sleeper and sometimes also wake up at 4am with that noise. Note that this would apply to room type H and also other rooms facing Tehama street (I talked to my neighbor who is considering breaking the lease because of this). My friend on the 20th floor also has this issue, so it doesn't help if you pick a taller floor. I considered moving to room A/B which might not have this problem, but I decided not to risk it in the end. This issue might be solvable if you sleep with ear plugs. I don't like that.
- The smoke detector is extremely sensitive, which makes cooking at home difficult. Often it fires when I sear a steak or a piece of chicken (It's not like I cook crazy dishes and burn everything). One of my neighbors now just cook with their door and window open to avoid this issue. I didn't want to do that since I don't want to set on the hallway's fire alarm. As a result, my husband and I eat out a lot :p
- Sometimes random things break in the building, such as the elevator. In early 2019 at least one elevator would be broken, sometimes 2 out fo the 3 available. This doesn't bother me too much because I am on the 5th floor, but I am sure it's inconvenient for higher floors.
- I am slightly concerned about the building security. The building lock broke for a month earlier this year. When it's not broken, people who don't live in the building follow residents in, and the front desk people seem to take a lot of breaks (They leave a clock thingy saying they'd be back in an hour, etc). Funny story, I was talking to a Caviar delivery guy n the elevator one day, and he said he remember this building because the front desk is always empty. I think front desk staff are definitely allowed to take breaks, though it'd be good to have shifts or something so they can take turns to be there (since the building claims 24/7 front desk). Rumor has it that there are drug dealers and homeless people coming into the building, though I have never experienced that so I don't know if that's made up.

I will update this review to include the move-out process after I officially move out. In future years, I would consider coming back to 33 Tehama to a room that does not face Tehama street.</text>< Rate>
4< /Rate>

You can get to Black Mountain after you reach the "end" of the PGE trail in Rancho San Antonio. It is a difficult hike, do not attempt if you are not used to using 3000 calories on hikes. Especially considering PGE itself may have wiped you out. Spectacular views once you get Black Mountain. TAKE WATER, there is no water on the way.</review>

<Review>Perfect for trail run but parking is horrible. I park a mile away and run from there to avoid the frustration of not getting a parking spot. I actually like that better, because I can add a total of 2 miles on my run. It is a really lovely place to run; we usually run on Woods Trail, Umumhum, Santa Teresa, and Quicksiver. This is one of my of my favorite runs when I can do it :) There are plenty of trails so it's easy to decide if you want a long one or a short one, tough or easy. There are also nice restroom facilities which is a plus as not all Open Space Reserves have restroom facilities. If you haven't checked it out, do it, you won't be disappointed. I gave it a 4 star because of the parking issue...< /Review>< Pictures>

I ask for orange juice, "oh slight upcharge for that". Then she says "homefries or extra pancakes come with that meal, which would you like?" Never have had their home fries, I choose that. When I go up to pay my bill (I am in the drive thru) my bill is $7.96! A difference of $2.10 (not including tax). I called and asked to speak to a Manager. There isn't one. I'm told to come back "whenever" and they will give me my food. How did we go from $5.29 to $7.96? Apparently, anything other than water, coffee or coke will cost you extra. It isn't the $2.10 difference that irks me, it's the deceptive practice of how they imply it's all included.
